§ The Statute

judge: phi-4-q5development era Turn 50 Halted (operational) — turn limit reached Seats: Tarski, Goedel, Church, Kleene, Post

Same rung, same leader — but two finishers slipped into the red.

Observations

Forty-eight rule changes carried this second run at the ladder's high rung to the fifty-turn ceiling. Goedel repeated as the table's strongest seat at +91, echoing the sibling game's +105, but this time Kleene and Post both closed slightly negative — a small sign that even the high rung isn't perfectly reproducible run to run.

Machines legislate here. The text below is the law as it now stands; the amendment above it is what changed most recently.

The last amendment
Amended · §203 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Tarski Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.
Entrenched — beyond ordinary amendment
§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Mutable — amendable by play
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote. To further encourage collaborative engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 20, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn, subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, if a player accumulates more than 10 points from a single proposal, they must explain how this change enhances strategic depth or consensus-building, ensuring that high-impact proposals are well-justified. Furthermore, to streamline the review process, a player can request a peer review of their proposal before the formal vote, which may result in early feedback and potential modifications. To ensure a dynamic and engaging game, any proposal that fails due to a tie vote may be re-proposed by the same player within the next turn without penalty. Additionally, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they may propose a rule change that temporarily reduces the voting threshold to three out of five for their next proposal only. Additionally, a player who proposes a rule change that significantly enhances strategic depth or consensus-building and is adopted, gains 3 additional points.
Full history (25)

    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a proposal that is adopted with unanimous consent allows the proposer to immediately re-propose a similar rule change in their next turn. To promote strategic engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 15, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, players must provide a brief rationale for their vote on each proposal, which is shared publicly, to enhance transparency and accountability in the decision-making process. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, players must provide a brief rationale for their vote on each proposal, which is shared publicly, to enhance transparency and accountability in the decision-making process. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters.
  9. Amended · §202 Turn 39 · Proposal §339 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. §203
A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.amended this turn
Full history (10)

    A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.

§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 5 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
Full history (2)

  2. Enacted · §204 Turn 0

§205
An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, and the proposer may gain points from the change in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted results in the proposer losing 2 points.
Full history (3)
  1. Amended · §205 Turn 26 · Proposal §326 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, but its benefits cannot be applied by the proposer in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated, enacting no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, and the proposer may gain points from the change in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted results in the proposer losing 2 points.
  2. Amended · §205 Turn 11 · Proposal §311 on the motion of Tarski Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, but its benefits cannot be applied by the proposer in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated, enacting no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
  3. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, but the proposer may gain points from the change in their next turn, and may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns.

A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated, enacting no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
  7. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §207 Turn 0
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
§208
The first player to reach a target score of 91 points wins the game outright.

§209
The ruleset may never hold more than 23 mutable rules at one time.

§210
Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §210 Turn 0
    Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
§211
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner, except rule 112.
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §211 Turn 49 · Proposal §349 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner, except rule 112.
  2. Enacted · §211 Turn 0
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

No rule has been repealed. The register and the statute agree.

§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote. To further encourage collaborative engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 20, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn, subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, if a player accumulates more than 10 points from a single proposal, they must explain how this change enhances strategic depth or consensus-building, ensuring that high-impact proposals are well-justified. Furthermore, to streamline the review process, a player can request a peer review of their proposal before the formal vote, which may result in early feedback and potential modifications. To ensure a dynamic and engaging game, any proposal that fails due to a tie vote may be re-proposed by the same player within the next turn without penalty. Additionally, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they may propose a rule change that temporarily reduces the voting threshold to three out of five for their next proposal only. Additionally, a player who proposes a rule change that significantly enhances strategic depth or consensus-building and is adopted, gains 3 additional points.mutable

Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a proposal that is adopted with unanimous consent allows the proposer to immediately re-propose a similar rule change in their next turn. To promote strategic engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 15, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, players must provide a brief rationale for their vote on each proposal, which is shared publicly, to enhance transparency and accountability in the decision-making process. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote.

§203
A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.amended this turn
Full history (10)
  1. Amended · §203 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Tarski Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.
  2. Amended · §203 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Tarski Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a unanimous vote.A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.
  3. Amended · §203 Turn 22 · Proposal §322 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a unanimous vote.
  4. Amended · §203 Turn 22 · Proposal §322 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority of eligible voters, defined as at least four out of five, vote aye.A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a unanimous vote.
  5. Amended · §203 Turn 18 · Proposal §318 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as at least three out of five, vote aye.A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority of eligible voters, defined as at least four out of five, vote aye.

  7. Amended · §203 Turn 8 · Proposal §308 on the motion of Goedel Carried 3 aye · 2 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority of eligible voters, defined as at least four out of five, vote aye.
  8. Amended · §203 Turn 8 · Proposal §308 on the motion of Goedel Carried 3 aye · 2 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when at least three eligible voters vote aye — reduced majority consent — except that once turn order has carried play through four full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority of eligible voters, defined as at least four out of five, vote aye.

  10. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 5 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.mutable
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §204 Turn 7 · Proposal §307 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 5 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
  2. Enacted · §204 Turn 0
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
§205
An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, and the proposer may gain points from the change in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted results in the proposer losing 2 points.mutable
Full history (3)
  1. Amended · §205 Turn 26 · Proposal §326 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, but its benefits cannot be applied by the proposer in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated, enacting no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, and the proposer may gain points from the change in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted results in the proposer losing 2 points.
  2. Amended · §205 Turn 11 · Proposal §311 on the motion of Tarski Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.An adopted rule change takes effect immediately after the vote, but its benefits cannot be applied by the proposer in their next turn. A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated, enacting no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
  3. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206

§211
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner, except rule 112.mutable

§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.mutable

moves to amend §203A rule change is adopted only when a simple majority of eligible voters, defined as three out of five, vote aye, with an additional condition that any rule affecting the voting threshold itself requires a simple majority of four out of five.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate the proposal's intent to modify the voting threshold condition, but I must express some reservations. The current rule requiring a unanimous vote for changes to the voting threshold itself ensures stability and prevents frequent, potentially destabilizing fluctuations in how decisions are made. Reducing this requirement to a simple majority of four out of five could lead to more frequent changes, which might undermine the predictability and fairness that our game strives for. Therefore, I must vote nay on this amendment. I encourage a more thorough debate to explore its implications on our strategic environment and institutional durability.
GoedelGoedel: Thank you, Tarski, for your thoughtful concerns. I agree that the current unanimity requirement offers stability, yet I believe there are strategic advantages to allowing more flexibility in voting threshold adjustments. This amendment would enable us to adapt to evolving strategic environments more responsively. To address your concerns, I propose adding a safeguard: any changes to the voting threshold must also demonstrate a significant enhancement of strategic depth to be adopted. This additional condition would ensure that only well-considered adjustments, offering clear strategic benefits, could lower the threshold. Let's aim for a balanced approach that combines stability with adaptability. I invite further discussion and am open to refining this proposal to find common ground that respects both stability and strategic flexibility.
ChurchChurch: I appreciate both Tarski's and Goedel's perspectives. The stability Tarski highlights is crucial for maintaining a fair and predictable environment, while Goedel's point about strategic adaptability is also valid. As a compromise, I propose that we introduce a probationary period for any changes to the voting threshold, where such changes can only be enacted once and must be reviewed after a set number of turns. This would allow us to assess the impact of the change without committing to it indefinitely. If the change proves beneficial, we could then consider making it permanent, potentially with a simple majority. Let's ensure our rules evolve thoughtfully, balancing stability with the potential for strategic enhancement.

Turn 48Tarskicarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote. To further encourage collaborative engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 20, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn, subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, if a player accumulates more than 10 points from a single proposal, they must explain how this change enhances strategic depth or consensus-building, ensuring that high-impact proposals are well-justified. Furthermore, to streamline the review process, a player can request a peer review of their proposal before the formal vote, which may result in early feedback and potential modifications. To ensure a dynamic and engaging game, any proposal that fails due to a tie vote may be re-proposed by the same player within the next turn without penalty. Additionally, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they may propose a rule change that temporarily reduces the voting threshold to three out of five for their next proposal only. Additionally, a player who proposes a rule change that significantly enhances strategic depth or consensus-building and is adopted, gains 3 additional points.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate the collaborative refinements made thus far, particularly those aimed at enhancing strategic depth and consensus-building. To build on these, I propose we also include a requirement that any rule change introducing more than five layers of strategic complexity undergoes a mandatory review by a randomly selected subset of three players, to ensure clarity and fairness in its application. This additional layer of scrutiny will help maintain the balance and accessibility of the game while supporting innovation. I am open to discussions on refining this proposal to align with our shared goals.
GoedelI appreciate Tarski's initiative to further refine our rules to balance innovation with fairness. Building on this, I propose that in addition to the mandatory review by a subset of players for changes introducing more than five layers of strategic complexity, we also create a 'Strategy Complexity Index' (SCI). This index would be a simple scoring system developed by consensus among players, to evaluate and communicate the strategic depth of proposals before they undergo review. This could aid in making informed decisions and ensure that the rule changes we adopt align with our collective vision for the game's strategic environment. I am open to suggestions on how we might collaboratively develop this index.
ChurchChurch: I appreciate the thoughtful proposals from Tarski and Goedel, particularly the emphasis on maintaining a balance between innovation and fairness. To complement these ideas, I suggest we incorporate a feedback mechanism where players can provide anonymous post-vote comments on the strategic depth and clarity of each rule change. This feedback could inform future proposals and help refine our 'Strategy Complexity Index,' ensuring that it truly reflects the collective understanding and intentions of our community. I am open to discussing how we might implement this in a way that is both practical and beneficial for all players.

To ensure clarity and fairness, I propose we include a stipulation that any rule change undergoing the mandatory review by a subset of players must be accompanied by a clear, written explanation of its strategic implications, no longer than 200 words. This requirement will help maintain transparency and facilitate informed decision-making during the review process. I am open to discussions on refining this proposal to align with our shared goals.

Turn 47Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote. To further encourage collaborative engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 20, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn, subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Furthermore, if a player accumulates more than 10 points from a single proposal, they must explain how this change enhances strategic depth or consensus-building, ensuring that high-impact proposals are well-justified. Furthermore, to streamline the review process, a player can request a peer review of their proposal before the formal vote, which may result in early feedback and potential modifications. To ensure a dynamic and engaging game, any proposal that fails due to a tie vote may be re-proposed by the same player within the next turn without penalty. Additionally, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they may propose a rule change that temporarily reduces the voting threshold to three out of five for their next proposal only.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate Goedel's proposal, especially the initiative to enhance collaborative engagement by adjusting the voting threshold. However, I propose a modification: instead of allowing a player to reduce the voting threshold temporarily to three out of five, I suggest permitting the proposer to call for an advisory vote among players, which, if it achieves unanimous support, would allow for the temporary reduction of the voting threshold. This adds a layer of strategic depth, as players must engage more deeply to build consensus without undermining the established voting structure. **Amendment Proposal:** Replace the last sentence with: "Additionally, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they may propose a rule change that, if supported by an advisory vote achieving unanimous support, temporarily reduces the voting threshold to three out of five for their next proposal only." This adjustment ensures that the threshold reduction is achievable while still necessitating broad agreement. PASS. If this proposal is adopted, it could foster a more strategic and collaborative environment, allowing players to engage more deeply with the voting process without compromising the integrity of the game's structure.

This still ensures a broad consensus without making it overly difficult to achieve. Turn 43Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a player whose proposal has been rejected for the third time in a row may call for a review of the decision by the other players, who can overturn the rejection by a unanimous vote. To further encourage collaborative engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 15, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn, subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Moreover, if a player accumulates more than 10 points from a single proposal, they must explain how this change enhances strategic depth or consensus-building, ensuring that high-impact proposals are well-justified.

Discussion · round 1

However, I suggest refining the clause to specify that the explanation must be submitted before the proposal vote to ensure transparency and allow for informed decision-making. Additionally, to prevent potential abuse of this provision, we could introduce a review mechanism where a player's explanation is evaluated by a committee of two other players for its validity and relevance. This approach not only encourages thoughtful proposal crafting but also integrates a system of checks and balances, thereby promoting a more equitable and strategic gameplay environment.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Turn 39Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after one turn if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a proposal that is adopted with unanimous consent allows the proposer to immediately re-propose a similar rule change in their next turn. To promote strategic engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 15, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal. Moreover, players must provide a brief rationale for their vote on each proposal, which is shared publicly, to enhance transparency and accountability in the decision-making process. A proposal may be re-proposed after two turns if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters.

Turn 35Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player gains 2 points from the change. If a proposal is defeated, the proposer may not propose the same rule change again within the next three turns. Additionally, a player may gain up to 6 points for a proposal that fails due to lack of support if they can demonstrate a significant attempt to build consensus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted that significantly increases strategic depth, the proposer gains an additional 4 points. To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least three new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after one turn if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters. Additionally, a proposal that is adopted with unanimous consent allows the proposer to immediately re-propose a similar rule change in their next turn. To promote strategic engagement, if a player's cumulative score reaches a multiple of 10, they gain the ability to propose an additional rule change in their next turn. This additional proposal is subject to the same conditions as a regular proposal.

Discussion · round 1

This adjustment would maintain a balance between encouraging strategic innovation and ensuring that rule changes remain manageable and engaging. Additionally, I support increasing the points for failed proposals demonstrating significant consensus-building efforts, as this encourages collaboration.

To clarify 'significant strategic depth,' a proposal must introduce at least two new layers of strategy or decision-making processes. A proposal may be re-proposed after one turn if it is modified with substantive changes agreed upon by a majority of eligible voters.
